Each initiative brought significant changes, though some were more successful than others in their implementation.  Therefore, all four statements are correct.


**8. Consider the following regarding the  "Revolt of 1857":**

1. The annexation of Awadh was a significant contributing factor.
2. The introduction of the Enfield rifle played a role in triggering the revolt.
3.  The revolt was solely a military mutiny.
4. The revolt received widespread support across all sections of Indian society.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the causes and nature of the 1857 Revolt?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Statements 1 and 2 are accurate. The annexation of Awadh fueled resentment among sepoys and the population, and the greased cartridges of the Enfield rifle served as an immediate trigger. However, statement 3 is inaccurate; the revolt extended far beyond a military mutiny, involving various social groups and regions. Statement 4 is also inaccurate; while the revolt had widespread support, it wasn't uniform across all sections of Indian society.  Therefore only two of the statements are accurate.


**9. Consider the following regarding social reform movements in 19th-century India:**

1.  The Brahmo Samaj opposed idolatry and emphasized monotheism.
2.  The Arya Samaj promoted the Shuddhi movement.
3.  The Theosophical Society advocated for the revival of ancient religions.
4.  The Prarthana Samaj focused primarily on Muslim social reform.


How many of the above statements correctly reflect the aims and activities of the mentioned social reform movements?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Statements 1, 2, and 3 are correct. The Brahmo Samaj championed monotheism and opposed idolatry; the Arya Samaj actively promoted the Shuddhi movement for reconversion to Hinduism; and the Theosophical Society aimed to revive aspects of ancient Indian religions and philosophies. Statement 4 is incorrect; the Prarthana Samaj primarily focused on Hindu social reform. Therefore, three statements correctly reflect the movements' aims and activities.


These questions are designed to challenge even well-prepared candidates, requiring thorough knowledge of the facts and the ability to analyze complex historical information.  They emphasize factual recall, analysis, and evaluation skills, aligning with the requirements of a UPSC-style examination.

Here are some UPSC-style Multiple Choice Questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria:


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Arya Samaj:**

1. It primarily comprised trading castes.
2.  It was significantly more widespread than the Brahmo Samaj.
3. It advocated for inter-caste marriages and widow remarriage.
4. Dayananda Saraswati is credited with its founding.

How many of the above statements are factually accurate regarding the Arya Samaj?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially true. While the Arya Samaj did have members from trading castes, its social base was broader, encompassing various social groups seeking reform.  Statement 2 is false. The Brahmo Samaj, established earlier, had a wider geographical reach and influence than the Arya Samaj, which was primarily concentrated in certain regions of Punjab and Western Uttar Pradesh. Statements 3 and 4 are accurate.  The Arya Samaj strongly advocated for social reforms like inter-caste marriages and widow remarriage, challenging traditional Hindu social structures. Dayananda Saraswati is widely recognized as the founder of the Arya Samaj.  Therefore, only three statements are correct.


**2. Consider the following regarding the Shiromani Gurudwara Prabandhak Committee (SGPC):**

1.  It was formed in the late 19th century as a political offshoot of the Singh Sabhas.
2.  Its primary aim was to secure control of Sikh shrines from government-controlled committees.
3.  The Akali Dal emerged directly from within the SGPC to facilitate the reclamation of Sikh shrines.
4. The SGPC was legally granted control over Sikh Gurudwaras through the Sikh Gurudwaras Act of 1922.

Which of the above statements accurately reflect the historical development and function of the SGPC?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 2, 3, and 4
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 2 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The SGPC was formed in 1920, not in the late 19th century, as a direct outcome of the Akali Movement. Statement 2 is correct.  A core objective of the SGPC was to wrest control of Sikh religious institutions from committees perceived as being manipulated by the British government. Statement 3 is largely correct. The Akali Dal, while not directly originating *within* the SGPC, was closely linked to it and played a crucial role in the movement to reclaim Sikh shrines.  Statement 4 is correct. The Sikh Gurudwaras Act of 1922 legally vested control of Sikh Gurudwaras in the SGPC.  Therefore, statements 2, 3, and 4 are accurate.



**3. Consider the following figures associated with the Indian freedom struggle:**

1.  Vinoba Bhave, known for his involvement in satyagraha.
2.  Maulana Azad, a prominent figure in the Khilafat Movement.
3.  Bhagat Singh, a key figure in the revolutionary terrorist movement.
4.  Raja Rammohan Roy, associated with the Brahmo Samaj.

How many of the individuals listed above played significant roles in different facets of the Indian nationalist movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All four individuals played significant roles in different aspects of the Indian freedom struggle. Vinoba Bhave was a prominent leader of the Bhoodan movement and participated in various satyagrahas. Maulana Azad was a crucial leader of the Khilafat Movement and a key figure in the Indian National Congress. Bhagat Singh was a prominent revolutionary who actively participated in armed rebellion against British rule. Raja Rammohan Roy was a leading figure in the Brahmo Samaj, a significant social and religious reform movement that indirectly contributed to the rise of Indian nationalism.  Therefore, all four statements are correct.


**4. Consider the following statements about the Revolt of 1857:**

1.  The revolt was solely a Sepoy Mutiny.
2.  It was primarily motivated by religious grievances.
3.  Nana Saheb and Rani Lakshmibai were prominent participants.
4.  The revolt led directly to the complete end of the British East India Company's rule.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect aspects of the Revolt of 1857?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Revolt of 1857 was much more than a Sepoy Mutiny; it involved widespread participation from various sections of Indian society, including civilians, princes, and landowners. Statement 2 is partially true. While religious sentiments played a role, the revolt was also driven by socio-economic and political factors, including resentment against British policies.  Statement 3 is correct; Nana Saheb and Rani Lakshmibai were prominent figures in the revolt. Statement 4 is incorrect. The revolt led to the dissolution of the British East India Company and the transfer of power to the British Crown, but it did not immediately end British rule in India. Consequently, only two statements are accurate.


**5. Consider the following about the Awadh Kisan Sabha:**

1. It urged farmers to cultivate ‘Bedakhli’ land.
2. It advocated for the abolition of ‘hari’ and ‘begar’.
3.  It was primarily active in the Punjab region.
4. It was closely allied with the Indian National Congress.

How many of the above statements accurately describe the Awadh Kisan Sabha and its activities?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect; the Awadh Kisan Sabha actively encouraged farmers to *refuse* to cultivate ‘Bedakhli’ land (land illegally occupied by landlords). Statement 2 is correct. A key aim of the Sabha was to end the exploitative practices of ‘hari’ (forced labor) and ‘begar’ (unpaid labor). Statement 3 is incorrect. The Awadh Kisan Sabha operated primarily in the Awadh region (present-day Uttar Pradesh), not Punjab.  Statement 4 is partially true; while it had links with the Congress, its primary focus was on peasant issues. Therefore, only two statements accurately reflect the Awadh Kisan Sabha’s activities.


**6. Consider the following concerning the Brahmo Samaj:**

1.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy is considered its founder.
2.  It completely rejected the Vedas and Upanishads.
3.  It actively promoted widow remarriage.
4.  It had a limited presence outside Bengal.

How many of these statements correctly characterize the Brahmo Samaj?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Raja Ram Mohan Roy is widely recognized as the founder of the Brahmo Samaj. Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Brahmo Samaj sought to reform Hinduism, it did not completely reject the Vedas and Upanishads; rather, it reinterpreted them. Statement 3 is correct. The Brahmo Samaj was a strong advocate for widow remarriage and other social reforms.  Statement 4 is incorrect. The Brahmo Samaj, although originating in Bengal, expanded to other parts of India. Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 accurately describe the Brahmo Samaj.


**7. Consider the following statements about Jyotirao Phule's Satyashodhak Samaj:**

1.  It was established in 1873.
2.  Phule argued that Brahmins were descendants of ‘alien’ Aryans.
3.  Phule's work primarily focused on the Maratha identity.

Which of the above statements are accurate regarding the Satyashodhak Samaj?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Satyashodhak Samaj was indeed founded in 1873. Statement 2 is also correct.  Phule's critique of the Brahminical order included the assertion that they were descendants of 'alien' Aryans. Statement 3 is incorrect. While Phule's work did impact the Maratha community, his focus was broader, encompassing the upliftment of all oppressed castes and classes.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 accurately reflect Phule's work.


**8. Consider the following concerning the events of the 1920s:**

1.  The Khilafat Movement aimed to protect the Ottoman Caliphate.
2.  The Non-Cooperation Movement involved boycotts of British institutions.
3.  The Nehru Report proposed Dominion Status as India's next political goal.
4.  The Simon Commission's all-British composition led to widespread boycotts.

Which of the above statements accurately reflect significant events during the 1920s in India?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 2, 3, and 4
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4
(d) 1 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All four statements are accurate. The Khilafat Movement was a significant pan-Islamic movement to protect the Ottoman Caliphate against British and Allied actions. The Non-Cooperation Movement included boycotts of educational institutions, law courts, and other government bodies. The Nehru Report, drafted in 1928, proposed Dominion Status as the immediate next step towards India's self-governance. The Simon Commission, with its all-British membership, was widely boycotted due to the exclusion of Indians. Therefore, all four statements are correct.


**9. Consider the following individuals and their associations:**

1.  Henry Lawrence: British Resident of Lucknow.
2.  Dayananda Saraswati: Founder of the Brahmo Samaj.
3.  Jyotirao Phule: Founder of the Satyashodhak Samaj.
4.  Mahatma Gandhi: Leader of the Khilafat Movement.

How many of the above pairings of individuals and their correct associations are accurate?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Henry Lawrence was indeed the British Resident of Lucknow during a critical period. Statement 2 is incorrect. Dayananda Saraswati founded the Arya Samaj, not the Brahmo Samaj. Statement 3 is correct. Jyotirao Phule is correctly identified as the founder of the Satyashodhak Samaj. Statement 4 is partially correct.  While Gandhiji did support and become involved in the Khilafat Movement, it wasn’t solely *his* movement, having other important Muslim leaders. Therefore, only three pairings are accurate.


**10. Consider the following statements regarding the early nationalist movement (1885-1905):**

1. It primarily focused on armed rebellion.
2.  It relied heavily on petitions and constitutional methods.
3.  It had widespread grassroots support among the peasantry.
4.  Dadabhai Naoroji played a significant role.

How many of these statements accurately reflect the characteristics of the early nationalist movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The early nationalist movement primarily employed constitutional and non-violent methods, not armed rebellion.  Statement 2 is correct.  The early nationalists focused on petitions, constitutional agitation, and appeals to the British government. Statement 3 is incorrect. The early nationalist movement's support base was largely among the educated urban elite; it had limited reach among the peasantry. Statement 4 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji was a prominent figure in the early nationalist movement.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 4 are accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and test factual recall and analytical skills.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the English East India Company's operations in India:**

1.  The Company established its first factory in Surat.
2.  The Company's headquarters were initially located in Masulipatnam.
3.  The Company monopolised the trade of Bengal.
4.  The Company received supplies from Bengal.
5. The Company's expansion was primarily driven by trade interests

How many of the above statements are factually accurate?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) Only four


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The English East India Company established its first factory in Surat in 1608, gaining a foothold in the lucrative Indian spice trade.  Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Company's initial headquarters were in Surat, later shifting to Madras, then Calcutta (Fort William). Statement 3 is largely correct, reflecting the Company's significant control over Bengal's trade, especially in textiles and other goods, although it didn't hold a complete monopoly in all aspects of trade. Statement 4 is correct. Bengal was a crucial source of revenue and supplies for the Company.  Statement 5 is correct. The Company's expansion was fundamentally driven by its pursuit of trade interests, though political and military influence became increasingly important over time. Therefore, four out of the five statements are factually accurate.


**2. Consider the following regarding the role of Henry Lawrence:**

1. Henry Lawrence was the British Resident in Lucknow.
2. He presided over the Regency Council after the Treaty of Bhairowal.
3. The Treaty of Lahore led to his appointment as a key official.
4. He died in a battle in Lucknow.

How many of the above statements accurately describe Henry Lawrence's career?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct; Henry Lawrence served as the British Resident in Lucknow. Statement 2 is correct; he played a significant role in the Regency Council following the Treaty of Bhairowal. Statement 3 is correct; the Treaty of Lahore influenced his appointments and responsibilities in the Punjab. Statement 4 is partially correct; while he did die in Lucknow, it wasn't during a battle, but during the Siege of Lucknow in the Indian Rebellion of 1857.  Therefore, three statements accurately reflect aspects of his career.


**3. Consider the following about the Sannyasi and Fakir uprisings:**

1. Warren Hastings issued a proclamation in 1773 banning Sannyasis from Bengal.
2. The uprisings were primarily contemporaneous with the Non-Cooperation Movement.
3.  The uprisings involved skirmishes between the English East India Company and religious groups.
4. Restrictions on the free movement of Sannyasis along pilgrimage routes contributed to the uprisings.


Which of the above statements accurately characterize the Sannyasi and Fakir uprisings?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1, 3, and 4
(c) 2 and 4
(d) 1 and 2


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Warren Hastings did issue such a proclamation, although the exact impact and enforcement are debated. Statement 2 is incorrect. The Sannyasi and Fakir uprisings predate the Non-Cooperation Movement by several decades. Statement 3 is correct. The uprisings were indeed characterized by conflicts between the Company and groups of Sannyasis and Fakirs. Statement 4 is correct. Restrictions on their movement were a significant factor in fueling the discontent that led to the uprisings. Therefore, statements 1, 3, and 4 accurately describe the Sannyasi and Fakir uprisings.


**4. Consider the following statements related to Ram Mohan Roy:**

1. He argued for monotheism in his work *Gift to Monotheism*.
2.  He attempted to isolate the moral and philosophical message of the New Testament in *Precepts of Jesus*.
3. He was a key figure in the establishment of the Bethune School.


Which of the above statements accurately reflect Ram Mohan Roy's contributions?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  *Gift to Monotheism* clearly presents Roy's arguments against polytheism. Statement 2 is correct. *Precepts of Jesus* reflects his attempt to separate the moral teachings from theological interpretations.  Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Roy was a significant figure in the reform movements that indirectly paved the way for women's education, he wasn't directly involved in founding the Bethune School. That was primarily the work of J.E.D. Bethune.  Therefore, only two statements are accurate.


**5. Consider the following about the annexation of Awadh:**

1. The annexation by Lord Dalhousie significantly impacted sepoy finances.
2. The annexation was a direct consequence of the Doctrine of Lapse.
3.  The annexation led to widespread unrest among the Awadh population.
4. Wajid Ali Shah was the Nawab of Awadh at the time of annexation.


How many of the above statements correctly describe the context and consequences of the annexation of Awadh?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The annexation destabilized the region and affected the economic well-being of many sepoys who had connections to Awadh. Statement 2 is partially correct. While the Doctrine of Lapse was a factor in Dalhousie's policies, the annexation of Awadh was based on the alleged misgovernance of Wajid Ali Shah, providing a pretext for annexation. Statement 3 is correct; the annexation naturally caused significant unrest and resentment among the Awadh populace. Statement 4 is correct; Wajid Ali Shah was indeed the Nawab at the time. Therefore, three statements accurately reflect the situation surrounding the annexation of Awadh.  The annexation wasn't solely a result of the Doctrine of Lapse, but rather a combination of factors, making option (d) incorrect.

**6. Consider the following regarding the impact of the English East India Company on Bengal:**

1. The Company's presence significantly affected Bengal's trade with Southeast Asia.
2. The Company's policies led to the decline of traditional industries in Bengal.
3. The Company introduced modern agricultural techniques that revolutionized Bengal's agriculture.
4. The Company's expansion in Bengal led to a significant increase in the region's overall prosperity.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the long-term impact of the English East India Company on Bengal?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. The Company's control over Bengal's ports and trade routes undeniably impacted its trade relations with Southeast Asia, although the nature and extent of the impact are complex and require deeper study. Statement 2 is correct. The Company's focus on raw materials for export and the introduction of British manufactured goods led to the decline of many traditional industries in Bengal. Statement 3 is incorrect. While some changes in agricultural practices occurred, they were not a widespread or successful modernization effort leading to revolutionary change. Statement 4 is incorrect. The Company's presence in Bengal, while leading to some economic growth for certain segments, ultimately resulted in the exploitation of resources and the impoverishment of many, especially the peasantry. Therefore, only two of the statements accurately reflect the long-term impact of the Company.


**7. Consider the following regarding the Non-Cooperation and Khilafat Movements:**

1. The movements adopted a program of non-violent non-cooperation.
2. The Khilafat issue was directly linked to immediate Indian political concerns.
3.  The movements saw significant participation from students and lawyers.
4. The Chauri Chaura incident led to the suspension of the movements.


How many of the above statements accurately characterize the Non-Cooperation and Khilafat Movements?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Non-violent non-cooperation was the central strategy. Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Khilafat issue served as a catalyst, the movements addressed broader Indian political grievances. Statement 3 is correct.  The movements witnessed large-scale participation from students and lawyers who boycotted institutions and gave up their practices, respectively. Statement 4 is correct. The Chauri Chaura incident played a crucial role in Gandhi's decision to suspend the movements. Therefore, three statements are accurate.


**8. Consider the following regarding the Government of India Act, 1935:**

1. The Act established provincial autonomy.
2. The Act created a fully independent federal legislature.
3.  The Act provided for universal adult suffrage.
4. The Act was widely accepted by the Indian National Congress.

How many of the above statements accurately describe the provisions of the Government of India Act, 1935?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Act did introduce a system of provincial autonomy. Statement 2 is incorrect. The federal legislature was not fully independent; significant powers remained with the Governor-General. Statement 3 is incorrect. The Act did not grant universal adult suffrage, it introduced a limited franchise. Statement 4 is incorrect. The Congress largely rejected the Act, considering it insufficient to address India's aspirations for self-governance.  Therefore, only one statement accurately describes the Act.


**9.  Consider the following regarding the individuals associated with Bengal:**

1.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj.
2.  Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj.
3.  Rabindranath Tagore was a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj.
4.  Subhas Chandra Bose was a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj.


How many of the above individuals were significantly associated with the Brahmo Samaj movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a founder and a central figure in the Brahmo Samaj movement.  Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar, Rabindranath Tagore, and Subhas Chandra Bose were prominent figures in Bengali society and the Indian nationalist movement, but their association with the Brahmo Samaj was not as direct or central to their identities. Therefore, only one of the statements is correct.


**10. Consider the following regarding the events in Bihar:**

1. The Champaran Satyagraha took place in Bihar.
2.  The Quit India Movement had minimal impact on Bihar.
3.  Kunwar Singh was a prominent leader of the 1857 revolt in Bihar.
4.  The establishment of the Kashi Vidyapith was a direct consequence of the Non-Cooperation Movement in Bihar.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the historical events in Bihar?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha was a significant event in Bihar's history. Statement 2 is incorrect. The Quit India Movement had a notable presence in Bihar. Statement 3 is correct. Kunwar Singh's leadership was crucial to the 1857 revolt in Bihar. Statement 4 is incorrect. While the Non-Cooperation Movement influenced the establishment of many national educational institutions, the Kashi Vidyapith is specifically associated with Varanasi (Kashi) in Uttar Pradesh, not Bihar. Therefore, three statements are factually accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, focusing on Lord Dalhousie's policies and their impact:


**1. Consider the following policies implemented during Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General of India:**

1.  Doctrine of Lapse
2.  Subsidiary Alliance System
3.  Direct annexation of territories based on alleged misgovernance
4.  Policy of extending pensions to adopted heirs of deceased rulers

How many of the above policies contributed to the expansion of British territories in India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Doctrine of Lapse, a key instrument of Dalhousie's annexation policy, led to the absorption of several princely states lacking natural heirs.  Direct annexation based on alleged misgovernance, as exemplified by the annexation of Awadh, further expanded British control.  The Subsidiary Alliance, while not a direct annexation policy in itself, paved the way for British influence and eventual control over many states.  Option 4 is incorrect; Dalhousie's policy explicitly *rejected* the traditional practice of recognizing adopted heirs, leading to annexations.  Therefore, three of the listed policies directly or indirectly contributed to territorial expansion.


**2. Consider the following statements regarding the annexation of Awadh under Lord Dalhousie:**

1.  The annexation was primarily driven by the desire to access Awadh's resources and its potential as a market for British goods.
2.  The Nawab of Awadh was deposed due to his lack of a natural heir, as per the Doctrine of Lapse.
3.  The annexation adversely affected the financial conditions of the sepoys stationed in Awadh.
4.  The annexation was justified on the grounds of misgovernance and the Nawab's refusal to implement reforms.

Which of the statements above accurately reflect the historical context of the annexation of Awadh?

(a) 1, 3, and 4
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately reflects the underlying economic motives behind the annexation. Dalhousie's "philanthropic" concerns masked the desire to exploit Awadh's resources and market potential. Statement 2 is incorrect; the Doctrine of Lapse did not apply as the Nawab had heirs. Statement 3 is plausible, although not explicitly detailed in all sources, the disruption caused by annexation likely impacted sepoys’ financial situations. Statement 4 correctly identifies the official justification used by Dalhousie to annex Awadh. Therefore, statements 1, 3, and 4 provide an accurate representation.


**3. Consider the following entities associated with Lord Dalhousie's administration:**

1.  Nawab Wajid Ali Shah
2.  Nana Saheb
3.  Sleeman
4.  Lord Canning

How many of the above individuals were directly or indirectly affected by Lord Dalhousie's policies of annexation and the Doctrine of Lapse?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Nawab Wajid Ali Shah was directly affected, being deposed and his kingdom annexed. Nana Saheb, the adopted son of the ex-Peshwa, was denied his pension, a consequence of Dalhousie's policies. Sleeman served as a key figure reporting to Dalhousie and was instrumental in assessing the situation leading to the annexation of various states. Lord Canning succeeded Dalhousie, inheriting the consequences of his annexation policies and facing the repercussions of the 1857 rebellion partly fueled by these actions.  Therefore, all four individuals were significantly impacted.


**4. Consider the following consequences of Lord Dalhousie's annexation policies:**

1.  Increased British control over Indian territories.
2.  Widespread economic disruption in annexed states.
3.  Strengthened the loyalty of Indian princes towards the British.
4.  Contributed to the growing resentment among Indians that ultimately culminated in the 1857 rebellion.

Which of the above statements correctly describe the effects of Dalhousie's policies?

(a) 1, 2, and 4
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 2, and 4 correctly reflect the outcomes of Dalhousie's aggressive annexation policies. The annexations demonstrably increased British territorial control and caused economic instability in the affected regions.  The policies also fueled resentment among the Indian population, contributing to the widespread discontent that erupted in 1857. Statement 3 is incorrect; the annexations and the Doctrine of Lapse significantly eroded trust and loyalty among Indian princes towards the British.  Therefore, only 1, 2, and 4 accurately reflect the consequences.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding Lord Dalhousie’s administrative actions:**

1. He annexed Punjab.
2. He implemented the Doctrine of Lapse.
3. He advocated for vernacular education.
4. He was the predecessor of Lord Curzon.

How many of the above statements are accurate regarding Lord Dalhousie’s actions and policies?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 2, and 3 are accurate. Lord Dalhousie annexed the Punjab following the Second Anglo-Sikh War. He famously implemented the Doctrine of Lapse, a policy leading to the annexation of several Indian states. He also supported vernacular education, although his overall approach to education was complex and not solely focused on vernacular systems. Statement 4 is incorrect; Lord Dalhousie was succeeded by Lord Canning, not Lord Curzon. Therefore, three statements are accurate.


**6. Consider the following territories annexed by Lord Dalhousie:**

1.  Satara
2.  Berar
3.  Sindh
4.  Awadh

How many of the above territories were annexed during Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Satara and Awadh were directly annexed under Dalhousie's rule, using the Doctrine of Lapse and alleged misgovernance as pretexts, respectively.  Berar was also acquired, though through a different arrangement involving the Nizam. Sindh's annexation predates Dalhousie's governorship. Therefore, three of the listed territories were annexed during his time.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions focus on factual recall, analysis, and evaluation, with a difficulty level designed to challenge UPSC aspirants.


**1. Consider the following regarding the 1857 Revolt:**

1. The revolt was solely a consequence of sepoy discontent.
2. Economic exploitation significantly fueled popular discontent.
3. The annexation of Awadh played a crucial role in escalating tensions.
4.  The British's perceived invincibility remained unchallenged before the revolt.

How many of the above statements are NOT accurate representations of the causes and context of the 1857 Revolt?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the sepoy mutiny was a trigger, the 1857 Revolt was a much broader uprising stemming from accumulated grievances across various sections of Indian society, including peasants, artisans, and zamindars.  It wasn't solely about sepoy discontent.

Statement 2 is accurate. The text explicitly highlights the economic exploitation of India by the British as a major factor contributing to widespread discontent and ultimately the revolt.

Statement 3 is accurate. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie in 1856 is described as a pivotal event that significantly increased resentment, particularly among sepoys from that region, and contributed to the atmosphere of rebellion.

Statement 4 is incorrect. The text mentions British military setbacks in the First Afghan War, the Punjab Wars, and the Crimean War, which eroded the perception of British invincibility and emboldened Indians to believe that British rule could be challenged. The Santhal rebellion further demonstrated the potential for successful uprisings against the British.

Therefore, statements 1 and 4 are inaccurate, making (c) the correct answer.


**2. Consider the following individuals and their contributions:**

1. Savitribai Phule:  Established the first girls' school in Pune.
2. Jyotiba Phule:  A key figure in the widow remarriage movement in Maharashtra.
3. Gopal Hari Deshmukh:  Known for advocating rational principles in social reform.
4. Dadabhai Naoroji:  Founder of the Parsi Law Association.

How many of the above correctly link the individuals with their primary contributions as described in the provided text?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The text explicitly mentions Savitribai Phule and her husband starting a girls' school in Pune in 1851.

Statement 2 is correct. While Jyotiba Phule is mentioned as a pioneer of the widow remarriage movement, the text also credits Vishnu Shastri Pundit and Karsondas Mulji with significant contributions to this movement.  Therefore, it's not entirely accurate to say he was the *key* figure.  However, his involvement is sufficiently established in the text for the statement to be considered largely correct within the context of the question.

Statement 3 is correct. Gopal Hari Deshmukh, known as "Lokahitawadi," is specifically mentioned for his advocacy of social reform based on rational principles and modern values.

Statement 4 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji's involvement in founding the Parsi Law Association, which worked for women's rights and legal reforms, is clearly stated in the text.

Therefore, three of the four statements correctly link individuals with their contributions, making (c) the correct answer.


**3. Consider the following regarding early nationalist organizations:**

1. The British India Association was the first public association in modern India.
2. The Landholders' Society primarily focused on promoting the interests of landlords.
3. The Indian Association was an all-India organization from its inception.
4. The East India Association was founded in India to influence British opinion.

How many of the statements above accurately reflect the characteristics and activities of early nationalist organizations in India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Landholders' Society, founded in 1837, predates the British India Association.

Statement 2 is correct. The Landholders' Society's primary aim was to advance the interests of landlords in Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Indian Association, while influential and aiming for all-India reach, initially operated mainly in Bengal.  It did not achieve all-India status immediately.

Statement 4 is incorrect. The East India Association, founded by Dadabhai Naoroji, was established in London to influence British public opinion and policymakers regarding Indian issues.

Therefore, only statements 2 is correct, making (b) the correct answer.


**4. Consider the following statements about the "safety valve" theory:**

1. A.O. Hume believed the Indian National Congress would prevent a violent uprising.
2. The theory fully explains the motivations behind the founding of the Indian National Congress.
3. The theory suggests the Congress was solely a tool for diverting popular discontent.
4.  The Wasudeo Balwant Phadke uprising exemplified the need for a "safety valve."

How many of the above statements accurately reflect aspects of the "safety valve" theory and its context?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The text indicates that Hume, in part, aimed to provide a peaceful outlet for growing discontent, preventing a potential violent rebellion.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The "safety valve" theory is presented as only *part* of the truth behind the Congress's founding; other, more noble motivations are also mentioned.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the theory suggests the Congress could serve as a means of channeling discontent, it doesn't portray it as solely a tool for manipulation. The text highlights the Congress's genuine pursuit of Indian political and economic advancement.

Statement 4 is correct.  The Phadke uprising is cited as an example of the growing unrest and the potential for armed rebellion, which further supports the rationale behind the "safety valve" concept.

Therefore, statements 1 and 4 accurately reflect aspects of the theory, making (b) the correct answer.


**5. Consider the following regarding individuals associated with the Home Rule Movement:**

1. Annie Besant played a significant leadership role.
2. Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a staunch opponent of the movement.
3. The movement aimed to achieve complete independence from British rule.
4. The movement directly led to the Non-Cooperation Movement.


How many of the above statements accurately describe the Home Rule Movement and the individuals involved?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct; Annie Besant is explicitly identified as a leader of the Home Rule Movement.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The text clearly indicates that Bal Gangadhar Tilak was also a leader in the Home Rule Movement, collaborating with Annie Besant.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Home Rule Movement pushed for greater self-governance, the text doesn't explicitly state that its aim was complete independence.  The ultimate goal of the movement is not definitively characterized as complete independence in the provided text.

Statement 4 is incorrect. While the Home Rule Movement contributed to the growth of nationalist sentiment, there's no direct causal link established in the text between the Home Rule Movement and the Non-Cooperation Movement.


Therefore, only statements 1 is definitively correct, making (b) the correct answer.  Note that statement 2 is incorrect, and statements 3 and 4 are not explicitly supported by the provided text.


**6. Consider the following concerning Aurangzeb's reign:**

1.  He consistently followed a policy of religious tolerance.
2.  His Deccan policy significantly contributed to the decline of the Mughal Empire.
3.  He maintained strong relations with the Rajputs throughout his rule.
4.  He abolished the *jizya* tax permanently.

How many of the above statements inaccurately characterize aspects of Aurangzeb's reign and policies?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Aurangzeb's reign is characterized by a stricter enforcement of Islamic law and policies that alienated many non-Muslim groups.  His actions towards Hindus and other religious groups are described as persecution and destruction of temples.

Statement 2 is largely correct.  The text suggests that Aurangzeb's Deccan policies, including prolonged military campaigns, contributed to the weakening of the Mughal Empire.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While he initially had relations with some Rajput rulers, his policies often led to conflict and antagonism.

Statement 4 is incorrect. The text indicates that Aurangzeb re-imposed the *jizya* tax, not abolished it permanently.

Therefore, three of the four statements inaccurately reflect Aurangzeb's reign, making (c) the correct answer.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, focusing on factual recall, analysis, and evaluation, with detailed explanations:


**1. Consider the following regarding the early phases of the Indian nationalist movement (1885-1905):**

1.  Advocated constitutional agitation within legal boundaries.
2.  Focused on building Indian public opinion and educating the British public about India's needs.
3.  Initially emphasized loyalty to British rule while aiming for gradual reforms.
4.  Successfully secured all major reforms demanded during this period.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the characteristics of the Moderate nationalists' approach?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Moderate nationalists primarily employed constitutional methods, petitioning, and public awareness campaigns to pressure the British government for reforms.  Their strategy involved both educating the Indian populace about political issues and influencing British public opinion to gain support for their cause.  Initially, many Moderates expressed loyalty to the Crown, believing that gradual change within the existing system was the most effective path. However, statement 4 is incorrect.  While they achieved some successes, the Moderates did not secure all of their major demands during this period.  Many significant reforms remained unrealized, leading to the rise of more radical approaches later on.


**2. Consider the following statements about the Anti-Partition Movement (Swadeshi and Boycott Movement):**

1.  The movement was solely led by militant nationalists like Tilak, Bipin Chandra Pal, and Aurobindo Ghose.
2.  Swadeshi involved the promotion of Indian goods and the boycott of British products.
3.  The movement saw significant participation from students, who faced government repression.
4.  The movement effectively involved and mobilized the peasantry of Bengal on a large scale.

How many of the above statements are accurate representations of the Anti-Partition Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While militant nationalists played a crucial role in later stages, the initial phase of the movement was led by moderate leaders as well, who worked in cooperation with the more radical elements. Statement 2 accurately describes the core of the Swadeshi movement – promoting Indian products and boycotting British goods. Statement 3 is correct; students actively participated and faced significant repression from the British authorities. Statement 4 is incorrect; while the movement had widespread support, its impact on the peasantry of Bengal remained limited, primarily affecting urban middle and lower-middle classes.


**3. Consider the following individuals associated with the Indian nationalist movement:**

1.  Dadabhai Naoroji
2.  Gokhale
3.  Lala Lajpat Rai
4.  Khudiram Bose

Which of the above individuals were primarily associated with the Moderate phase of the nationalist movement?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 1, 2, and 4
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji and Gopal Krishna Gokhale were prominent leaders of the Moderate phase of the Indian National Congress.  They championed constitutional methods and worked within the legal framework to achieve gradual reforms. Lala Lajpat Rai, while initially a moderate, later leaned towards the more radical wing of the movement. Khudiram Bose was a prominent revolutionary terrorist, actively involved in violent acts against British rule, placing him firmly outside the moderate camp.


**4. Consider the following regarding the consequences of the Anti-Partition Movement:**

1.  A significant rise in revolutionary terrorism.
2.  The emergence of national educational institutions.
3.  A flourishing of nationalist literature, poetry, and journalism.
4.  The complete and immediate success in reversing the partition of Bengal.

How many of the above were direct consequences of the Anti-Partition Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Anti-Partition Movement led to a surge in revolutionary terrorism as a response to government repression and the perceived failure of moderate approaches. The movement spurred the creation of national educational institutions as a way to counter the perceived denationalizing effects of the British education system.  A notable upswing in nationalist literature, poetry, and journalism also occurred. However, statement 4 is incorrect. While the partition was eventually annulled, it wasn't an immediate consequence of the movement; it took several years and further political developments.


**5. Consider the following aspects of the early nationalist movement:**

1.  The emphasis on creating a strong national identity and consciousness among Indians.
2.  The significant role played by the Indian press in disseminating nationalist ideas and mobilizing public opinion.
3.  The complete absence of any economic dimension in the nationalists' demands and strategies.
4.  The reliance on constitutional methods and petitions as the primary means of political engagement with the British government.

How many of the statements above accurately reflect the characteristics of the early nationalist movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The early nationalist movement successfully fostered a sense of shared Indian identity and nationalism. The Indian press played a crucial role in spreading nationalist ideas and mobilizing public support.  The movement also utilized constitutional methods and petitions. However, statement 3 is incorrect.  The early nationalists' concerns were not limited to political issues; they also addressed the economic exploitation of India by British rule, highlighting the economic dimension of British imperialism.


**6. Consider the following about the Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909:**

1. Increased the number of elected members in the Imperial Legislative Council and provincial councils.
2.  Introduced direct elections for all members of the Imperial Legislative Council.
3.  Granted complete self-government or Swaraj to India.
4.  Reserved some elected seats for landlords and British capitalists in India.

How many of the above statements correctly describe aspects of the Morley-Minto Reforms?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Morley-Minto Reforms did increase the number of elected members in legislative councils but did not introduce direct elections for all members.  The reforms certainly did not grant self-government; it was a far cry from the nationalists' demands.  However, the reforms did reserve some seats for landlords and British capitalists, aiming to co-opt certain segments of Indian society and maintain British control.


**7. Consider the following regarding Mahatma Gandhi's influence:**

1. Inspired Rani Gaidinliu's rebellion against British rule.
2.  Led the Dandi March as part of the Second Civil Disobedience Movement.
3.  Negotiated the Gandhi-Irwin Pact.
4.  Completely succeeded in preventing the Partition of India.


How many of the above statements accurately reflect Gandhi's actions and impact?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Gandhi's philosophy and actions significantly influenced Rani Gaidinliu's participation in the independence movement. He led the Dandi March, a pivotal moment in the Second Civil Disobedience Movement.  He also negotiated the Gandhi-Irwin Pact.  However, statement 4 is incorrect. While Gandhi made significant efforts to mitigate the consequences of partition, he ultimately could not prevent it.


**8. Consider the following figures associated with revolutionary terrorism:**

1.  Khudiram Bose
2.  V.D. Savarkar
3.  Gokhale
4.  Aurobindo Ghose


How many of the above were directly involved in revolutionary terrorist activities or organizations?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Khudiram Bose was a key figure in the revolutionary terrorist movement, directly involved in acts of violence against British officials. V.D. Savarkar was a prominent figure in the Hindu Mahasabha and also actively involved in revolutionary activities, organizing secret societies.  Gokhale and Aurobindo Ghose, while significant figures in the nationalist movement, were not directly involved in revolutionary terrorism, with Aurobindo Ghose shifting towards spiritual pursuits later.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Bal Gangadhar Tilak, Jawaharlal Nehru, the Quit India Movement, and related historical events and figures.  The questions aim for a high difficulty level with plausible distractors.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding Bal Gangadhar Tilak's political activities:**

1. He actively participated in the anti-cow slaughter campaigns.
2. He vehemently opposed the Montford Reforms.
3. He was a key figure in the 1899 Bombay textile strike.
4. He was instrumental in bringing lower castes into the Indian National Congress.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect aspects of Tilak's political career?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 3, and 4 are accurate.  Tilak's advocacy extended to various social issues, including the protection of cows, a significant aspect of Hindu identity. His involvement in the 1899 Bombay textile strike showcased his concern for workers' rights and his ability to mobilize support across social strata.  His efforts significantly broadened the Congress's base, including lower castes.  However, while Tilak was critical of certain aspects of British rule and the inadequacies of reforms,  his opposition to the Montford Reforms (which aimed at limited self-governance) wasn't as absolute or prominent as his other actions. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the nuances of Tilak's multifaceted political engagement.  Options (a), (b), and (d) introduce plausible distractors, testing the candidate's ability to differentiate between strong and weaker aspects of Tilak’s legacy.


**2. Consider the following individuals associated with the Indian National Movement:**

1.  Sir Tej Bahadur Sapru
2.  P.C. Joshi
3.  Sarojini Naidu
4.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale

Which of the above were known primarily for their association with the "moderate" faction of the Indian National Congress during its early years?

(a) 1 and 4 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4
(d) 1, 2, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Sir Tej Bahadur Sapru and Gopal Krishna Gokhale are correctly identified as prominent figures of the moderate wing of the Indian National Congress. Their approach emphasized constitutional methods, petitions, and gradual reform within the existing political framework.  P.C. Joshi was a prominent communist leader, and Sarojini Naidu, while a significant Congress figure, was more aligned with the nationalist movement's broader spectrum rather than being solely identified with the moderates.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of the factional dynamics within the Congress. The distractors in options (b), (c), and (d) include individuals associated with other ideological strands of the freedom struggle, making the question challenging.


**3. Consider the following statements about the Quit India Movement:**

1.  The movement was launched on August 9, 1942.
2.  Jayaprakash Narayan played a significant leadership role, particularly in Bihar.
3.  The movement received substantial support from the Princely States.
4.  The Communist Party of India actively participated in the movement's organizational efforts.

How many of these statements accurately describe the Quit India Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 2 are accurate. The Quit India Movement began on August 9, 1942, and Jayaprakash Narayan's leadership in Bihar was crucial to its success in that region.  However, statement 3 is incorrect; the Princely States largely remained aloof or even opposed to the movement, highlighting the limitations of the movement's reach.  Statement 4 is also incorrect; the Communist Party of India, due to its initial alignment with British war efforts, initially distanced itself from the Quit India Movement. This question assesses the candidate's understanding of the geographical and political nuances of the movement, including its limitations and the complexities of political alliances during that period. The options test the ability to recall specific facts and differentiate between active and passive participation in the movement.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding Jawaharlal Nehru's role in post-independence India:**

1. He played a crucial role in shaping India's foreign policy, emphasizing non-alignment.
2. He was a key figure in the drafting of the Objectives Resolution, which laid the foundation for the Indian Constitution.
3. He strongly opposed the partition of India and actively worked to prevent it.
4. He primarily focused on economic policies aligned with laissez-faire capitalism.


Which of the statements above accurately reflect Nehru's contributions to post-independence India?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 2, and 3 are accurate. Nehru's vision of non-alignment shaped India's international relations, his contribution to the Objectives Resolution was foundational to the Constitution, and while he accepted partition, he did not support it and tried to prevent it.  Statement 4 is incorrect; Nehru's economic policies leaned towards a mixed economy with socialist leanings, not laissez-faire capitalism. This question assesses the candidate's knowledge of Nehru's multifaceted role in post-independence India, including his foreign policy, constitutional contributions, and approach to economic development.  The options include distractors that test the candidate's ability to distinguish between Nehru's actual policies and potentially misleading interpretations.


**5. Consider the following publications and the individuals associated with them:**

1.  *Kesari* – Bal Gangadhar Tilak
2.  *Mahratta* – Gopal Ganesh Agarkar
3.  *India* – Dadabhai Naoroji
4.  *Yugantar* – Aurobindo Ghosh

How many of the pairings above correctly link a publication to its primary editor or founder during the Indian freedom struggle?


(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 3, and 4 are correct. *Kesari* was indeed founded and edited by Bal Gangadhar Tilak; *India* was a journal associated with Dadabhai Naoroji's efforts to promote India's cause in Britain; and *Yugantar* was a revolutionary newspaper associated with Aurobindo Ghosh.  However, *Mahratta* was primarily associated with Bal Gangadhar Tilak, not Gopal Ganesh Agarkar, although Agarkar did contribute to it. This question tests knowledge of important publications from the freedom struggle era and their association with key figures. The inclusion of a partially correct pairing (statement 2) makes the question more demanding.
