(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 3, and 4 accurately describe the Vaikom Satyagraha. It was indeed a significant campaign against untouchability and caste-based discrimination in Kerala. The Satyagraha was a key part of the broader Temple Entry Movement aiming at ending restrictions on Dalits' access to temples. However, statement 2 is incorrect; while Gandhi supported the movement, he did not directly lead the Vaikom Satyagraha.  Other leaders played a crucial role in its organization and execution.  Therefore, three statements are correct.


**9. Consider the following regarding the events leading up to and including the Quit India Movement:**

1. The Cripps Mission's failure further intensified the demand for Indian independence.
2.  The August Offer, while offering dominion status, failed to satisfy the Congress's demands.
3.  The Congress Working Committee's Wardha resolution unequivocally supported British war efforts.
4.  Individual Satyagraha was a significant precursor to the Quit India Movement.

How many of the above statements are correct in the context of the events leading to the Quit India Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 2, and 4 accurately reflect the historical sequence. The failure of the Cripps Mission to address the Congress's core demands for independence created a climate of deep frustration and intensified calls for immediate action.  The August Offer, while offering dominion status as a future goal, was deemed inadequate by the Congress, failing to address the demand for immediate self-rule. Individual Satyagraha, initiated by Gandhi, was a strategic step that escalated the pressure on the British and paved the way for the mass mobilization of the Quit India Movement.  However, Statement 3 is incorrect; the Wardha resolution did *not* unequivocally support British war efforts;  the Congress offered conditional support, linking it to the granting of independence.  Therefore, three statements are correct.


**10. Consider the following regarding the differences between the ideologies of Gandhi and Bose:**

1. Both leaders prioritized the attainment of complete independence for India.
2. Gandhi's emphasis on non-violence contrasted with Bose's willingness to explore alliances with the Axis powers.
3. Both leaders completely rejected socialism as a viable economic model for India.
4.  Both viewed religion as a divisive force and advocated for a completely secular state.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the ideological differences between Gandhi and Subhas Chandra Bose?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 2 correctly highlight key ideological differences. Both Gandhi and Bose shared the overarching goal of Indian independence. However, their approaches differed significantly. Gandhi's unwavering commitment to non-violent resistance contrasted sharply with Bose's pragmatism, which led him to explore alliances with the Axis powers, a move vehemently opposed by Gandhi. Statement 3 is incorrect; both leaders, while differing in their approaches, did in fact endorse some form of socialism, although their interpretations and application differed greatly. Statement 4 is also incorrect; while both were relatively secular in their outlook, neither completely rejected religion's role in society.  Therefore, only two statements accurately depict the ideological differences.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided historical data, aiming for a difficult level and incorporating diverse cognitive skills:


**1. Consider the following:**

1.  The advocacy of "Swaraj" as the ultimate goal of the Indian national movement.
2.  The utilization of traditional festivals like Ganapati and Shivaji festivals for political mobilization.
3.  The organization of national schools and colleges as an alternative to British educational institutions.
4.  The prominent role played by newspapers like *Kesari* and *Mahratta* in shaping nationalist opinion.
5. The significant contribution of the All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC) in the labour movement.

How many of the above were key characteristics or features of the Extremist phase of the Indian nationalist movement (1905-1909)?

(a) Only two
(b) Only three
(c) Only four
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Extremist phase of the Indian nationalist movement (1905-1909), spearheaded by figures like Bal Gangadhar Tilak, Lala Lajpat Rai, and Bipin Chandra Pal, was characterized by a distinct set of strategies and ideologies.  The demand for "Swaraj," initially interpreted differently by various leaders but ultimately signifying self-rule, was central to their agenda.  They cleverly leveraged existing cultural events like the Ganapati and Shivaji festivals to galvanize mass support and disseminate their message. The boycott of British-controlled educational institutions led to the creation of national schools and colleges, fostering a distinct Indian education system.  Publications like *Kesari* and *Mahratta*, edited by Tilak, played a crucial role in shaping public opinion and disseminating nationalist ideas. However, while the labour movement gained momentum during this period, the AITUC's formation postdates this specific era. Therefore, only four of the statements accurately reflect the characteristics of the Extremist phase between 1905 and 1909. Options (a) and (b) underestimate the breadth of the Extremists' activities, while option (d) incorrectly includes the AITUC's role within the specified timeframe.


**2. Consider the following personalities:**

1.  Lord Curzon
2.  Lord Minto
3.  Lord Morley
4.  Lord Hardinge
5.  Dadabhai Naoroji

How many of the above were directly involved in shaping the political landscape of India during the period of the Swadeshi movement and its immediate aftermath (roughly 1905-1911)?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Lord Curzon's policies, particularly the Partition of Bengal, directly triggered the Swadeshi movement. Lord Minto served as Viceroy during the height of the movement and played a crucial role in the negotiations leading to the Morley-Minto Reforms.  Lord Morley, as Secretary of State for India, was instrumental in formulating these reforms. Lord Hardinge, as Viceroy, witnessed the movement's decline and the rise of revolutionary terrorism, dealing with its aftermath. Dadabhai Naoroji's influence, though significant as a nationalist leader, was more indirect during this specific period.  He had already established his reputation before the Swadeshi movement. Therefore, four of the listed figures played direct roles in shaping India's political landscape during the period 1905-1911. Option (a) underestimates the involvement of key figures, while (c) and (d) are inaccurate in their inclusion or exclusion of specific individuals.



**3. Consider the following statements regarding the Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909:**

1.  They introduced the principle of separate electorates for Muslims.
2.  They significantly increased the number of directly elected members in the Imperial Legislative Council.
3.  They aimed to placate moderate nationalists while isolating extremist elements.
4.  They granted Indians substantial control over the budget of the government.
5.  They were largely successful in resolving the underlying tensions between Hindu and Muslim communities.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the key features and consequences of the Morley-Minto Reforms?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) Only four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Morley-Minto Reforms, enacted in 1909, were a significant development in the Indian political landscape.  The introduction of separate electorates for Muslims (1) was a key feature, albeit a divisive one. The reforms did increase the number of elected members in legislative councils (2) but the election process was indirect, limiting direct representation.  The reforms aimed to appease moderate nationalists while marginalizing extremist factions (3). However, the reforms didn't grant Indians significant budgetary control (4), and they ultimately failed to bridge the growing divide between Hindu and Muslim communities (5), instead exacerbating existing tensions.  Therefore, only three statements accurately describe the reforms.  Options (a), (b), and (d) either oversimplify or misrepresent the complex nature and effects of the reforms.


**4. Consider the following publications:**

1.  *Young India*
2.  *Kesari*
3.  *The Punjabee*
4.  *Hitabadi*
5.  *Mahratta*

How many of the above were significant newspapers or journals associated with the dissemination of nationalist ideas during the era of militant nationalism in India (roughly 1905-1910)?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Several newspapers played a crucial role in spreading nationalist ideas during the period of militant nationalism.  *Kesari* and *Mahratta*, both associated with Bal Gangadhar Tilak, were instrumental in shaping public opinion in Maharashtra.  *The Punjabee*, associated with Lala Lajpat Rai, played a similar role in Punjab. *Hitabadi* was a significant Bengali-language newspaper during the Swadeshi movement.  *Young India*, however, is primarily associated with Mahatma Gandhi's later phase of the nationalist movement.  Therefore, four of the listed publications were significant during the specified era. Options (a), (c), and (d) either incorrectly include or exclude publications based on their association with the period of militant nationalism.


**5. Consider the following individuals:**

1.  N.M. Joshi
2.  Joseph Baptista
3.  Maulana Abul Kalam Azad
4.  Lala Lajpat Rai
5.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak

How many of the above individuals were prominent figures in the Indian nationalist movement during the period encompassing the Swadeshi movement and the rise of revolutionary terrorism (roughly 1905-1917)?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five individuals listed played significant roles in the Indian nationalist movement during the specified period.  N.M. Joshi was a prominent labor leader, and his activities intersected with the broader nationalist movement. Joseph Baptista was involved in the Home Rule movement. Maulana Abul Kalam Azad was a key figure in the Congress, and his views on independence were influential. Lala Lajpat Rai and Bal Gangadhar Tilak were central figures in the Extremist wing of the nationalist movement, actively participating in the Swadeshi movement and facing government repression.  Therefore, all five were prominent figures during this tumultuous period.  All other options incorrectly exclude one or more key figures from the movement’s activities during this era.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, focusing on Jawaharlal Nehru, other key figures, and historiographical approaches to modern Indian history.  Each question adheres to the specified format and difficulty level, aiming to challenge the examinee's factual recall and analytical skills.


**1. Consider the following:**

1.  Championed the Scientific Policy Resolution.
2.  Headed the Council of Scientific and Industrial Research (CSIR).
3.  Encouraged the work of Homi J. Bhabha.
4.  Served as President of the Indian National Congress.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect Jawaharlal Nehru's roles and contributions to post-independence India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  Jawaharlal Nehru played a pivotal role in shaping India's scientific and technological development. He championed the Scientific Policy Resolution (SPR) in 1958, which aimed to integrate science and technology into national development. He also headed the CSIR, a key institution for promoting scientific research, and actively encouraged the work of Homi J. Bhabha, a leading figure in India's nuclear program. However, while Nehru held numerous positions of power within the Indian National Congress, he was never its President.  Therefore, statements 1, 2, and 3 are accurate, while 4 is incorrect.


**2. Consider the following statements regarding the Nehru Report (1928):**

1.  Proposed Dominion Status as the immediate political goal.
2.  Was unequivocally supported by Subhas Chandra Bose.
3.  Recommended joint electorates as a solution to communal representation.
4.  Was rejected outright by the Muslim League.

How many of these statements correctly characterize the Nehru Report and its reception?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The Nehru Report, drafted by Motilal Nehru, proposed Dominion Status as the immediate goal, although it also mentioned complete independence as a long-term aspiration.  It did recommend joint electorates, aiming for a unified electorate system.  The Muslim League, however, rejected the report due to its failure to adequately address Muslim concerns regarding separate electorates and representation.  Subhas Chandra Bose, known for his more radical stance, did not fully support the report's moderate approach.  Thus, statements 1, 3, and 4 are correct; statement 2 is incorrect.


**3. Consider the following individuals associated with the Indian independence movement:**

1.  M.A. Jinnah, who played a key role in the Pakistan Movement.
2.  Sardar Patel, known for his role in integrating princely states.
3.  C. Rajagopalachari, who served as the last Governor-General of India.
4.  Subhas Chandra Bose, who founded the Forward Bloc.

How many of the above individuals were actively involved in the political discourse surrounding the partition of India?


(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** All four individuals played significant roles in the period leading up to and including the partition of India.  M.A. Jinnah's leadership of the Muslim League was central to the creation of Pakistan. Sardar Patel's efforts in integrating princely states were crucial to post-partition India's consolidation. C. Rajagopalachari, although not directly involved in the partition negotiations, was a key figure in the Congress and held a significant position during this tumultuous period. Subhas Chandra Bose's ideology and actions, although separate from the mainstream Congress approach, also indirectly impacted the political climate and the eventual partition.


**4. Consider the following about the Khilafat Movement:**

1.  It was primarily concerned with the fate of the Ottoman Caliphate.
2.  It saw significant collaboration between Hindus and Muslims.
3.  It was entirely separate from the Non-Cooperation Movement.
4.  It led to widespread communal harmony across India.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect aspects of the Khilafat Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The Khilafat Movement was indeed deeply concerned with the fate of the Ottoman Caliphate and the treatment of Muslims in Turkey after World War I.  It also witnessed a period of significant collaboration between Hindus and Muslims under Gandhi's leadership. However, the movement wasn't entirely separate from the Non-Cooperation Movement; it ran concurrently and shared many participants and goals.  Finally, while the movement initially fostered Hindu-Muslim unity, it did not lead to *widespread* and lasting communal harmony across the entire country; tensions and conflicts remained.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are accurate.


**5. Consider the following regarding the Government of India Act, 1935:**

1.  Established an All-India Federation that ultimately came into being.
2.  Introduced provincial autonomy, replacing dyarchy.
3.  Completely eliminated the governor's special powers in the provinces.
4.  Resulted in the immediate grant of complete independence to India.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the features of the Government of India Act, 1935?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The Government of India Act, 1935, did indeed introduce provincial autonomy and replace dyarchy.  However, the proposed All-India Federation never materialized due to the non-participation of princely states.  Furthermore, the Act retained significant special powers for the governor in the provinces, acting as a check on the newly granted autonomy.  The Act did not grant complete independence; that came much later.  Therefore, only statements 2 is accurate.


**6.  Consider the following regarding the historiographical approaches to modern Indian history:**

1. The Colonial approach often praised Western culture and values.
2. The Nationalist approach emerged as a direct response to the Colonial approach.
3. The Marxist approach solely focuses on class struggle, ignoring other social factors.
4. The Subaltern approach emphasizes the voices of marginalized groups.


Which of the above statements accurately describe the characteristics of the mentioned historiographical approaches?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1, 2, and 4
(c) 2, 3, and 4
(d) 1, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Statements 1, 2, and 4 accurately reflect the characteristics of the mentioned historiographical approaches. The colonial approach often presented a biased view, glorifying British rule and criticizing Indian society and culture.  The nationalist approach developed as a counter-narrative to the colonial perspective, emphasizing the positive aspects of Indian culture and the struggle for independence. The Subaltern approach focuses on the experiences and perspectives of marginalized groups, challenging elite-centric narratives. However, the Marxist approach, while emphasizing class struggle, doesn't solely focus on it; it also considers other social and political factors in its analysis of historical events.  Therefore, only 1, 2, and 4 are correct.


**7. Consider the following about the Civil Disobedience Movement and its aftermath:**

1.  Gandhi advocated a "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy.
2.  Nehru initially supported office acceptance after the movement's withdrawal.
3.  The Congress won a majority in most provincial assemblies in the 1937 elections.
4.  The Government of India Act, 1935, was universally welcomed by Indian nationalists.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the events and debates surrounding the Civil Disobedience Movement and its aftermath?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Gandhi indeed advocated the "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy, aiming for periods of mass action interspersed with periods of negotiation and respite.  The Congress did win a majority in most provincial assemblies in the 1937 elections.  However, Nehru initially opposed office acceptance, advocating for continued mass struggle rather than participation in the legislative system established under the 1935 Act. The 1935 Act was not universally welcomed; it was largely rejected by the Congress, although other groups held differing views. Thus, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.



**8. Consider the following figures and their primary association with religious reform movements in India:**

1.  Dadabhai Naoroji – Parsis
2.  Sayyid Ahmad Khan – Muslims
3.  Swami Dayanand Saraswati – Sikhs
4.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy – Brahmo Samaj

How many of the above correctly match the individual with their prominent religious reform movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Dadabhai Naoroji was a key figure in Parsi religious reform, particularly through his involvement with the Rahnumai Mazdayasnan Sabha. Sayyid Ahmad Khan led significant reform efforts within the Muslim community. Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a founder of the Brahmo Samaj. However, Swami Dayanand Saraswati was associated with the Arya Samaj, not the Sikh reform movements. Therefore, only three of the pairings are correct.


**9. Consider the following about prominent figures in the Indian National Congress:**

1.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a prominent leader of the early Congress.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a staunch advocate of "Swaraj".
3.  Motilal Nehru authored the Nehru Report.
4.  Mahatma Gandhi exclusively focused on non-violent resistance throughout his career.

How many of the above statements are accurate regarding these figures and their roles?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a significant leader of the early, moderate phase of the Indian National Congress. Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a prominent figure advocating for "Swaraj" and a more assertive form of nationalism. Motilal Nehru did indeed author the Nehru Report. However, while Gandhi primarily employed non-violent methods,  there were instances where he did not rule out other forms of protest or pressure.  Therefore, three statements are accurate.


**10. Consider the following regarding the impact of British rule on India:**

1.  Lord Cornwallis implemented the Permanent Settlement.
2.  Lord Wellesley introduced the Subsidiary Alliance System.
3.  Sir John Shore is primarily associated with the Anglo-Nepal War.
4.  Lord Hastings oversaw the First Anglo-Maratha War.


How many of the above statements accurately reflect the administrative and military actions of the British in India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Lord Cornwallis is correctly linked to the Permanent Settlement of Bengal, a significant land revenue policy. Lord Wellesley implemented the Subsidiary Alliance System, a key strategy for expanding British influence.  Sir John Shore's governorship is linked to the beginning of  the Anglo-Nepalese War. However, Lord Hastings was associated with the *Third* Anglo-Maratha War, not the first. Three of the statements are therefore accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided information about the Indian National Congress, adhering to all specified criteria.  The difficulty level aims for "difficult" by incorporating subtle factual variations and plausible distractors.


**1. Consider the following regarding the early phases of the Indian National Congress:**

1.  The initial sessions were primarily attended by lawyers, journalists, and a few industrialists.
2.  The Congress initially focused on constitutional reforms and gradual changes within the existing system.
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji served as Congress President on three separate occasions.
4.  The "drain theory," highlighting British economic exploitation, was a key component of the early Congress's economic critique.
5.  Kadambini Ganguly's address to a Congress session in 1890 symbolized the early movement's commitment to women's rights.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the early phase (1885-1905) of the Indian National Congress?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five statements accurately reflect aspects of the Indian National Congress's early phase.  While the initial membership was predominantly composed of professionals like lawyers and journalists,  industrialists were also represented, making statement 1 correct.  The Congress's initial strategy of constitutional reform and gradual change is well documented, supporting statement 2. Dadabhai Naoroji's three terms as President are a matter of historical record (statement 3). The "drain theory," a crucial element of the economic critique of British rule, was indeed central to the early Congress's platform (statement 4). Finally, Kadambini Ganguly's address in 1890 is a significant event symbolizing the early movement's nascent inclusion of women (statement 5).  Therefore, all five statements are correct.



**2. Consider the following regarding the contrasting ideologies of Mahatma Gandhi and Subhas Chandra Bose:**

1.  Both leaders advocated for some form of socialism, although their interpretations differed significantly.
2.  Gandhi's Hind Swaraj emphasized a decentralized, stateless society, while Bose's vision leaned towards a more centralized, potentially authoritarian state, at least initially.
3.  Bose strongly believed in the efficacy of violent resistance, contrasting with Gandhi's unwavering commitment to non-violent methods.
4.  While both opposed untouchability, their approaches and emphasis varied. Gandhi's focus was on reforming the caste system while Bose favored its abolition.
5. Both leaders consistently rejected communism and fascism as viable ideologies for India.


How many of these statements accurately reflect the ideological differences between Gandhi and Bose?

(a) Only two
(b) Only three
(c) Only four
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Four of the statements accurately capture the key ideological differences. Statements 1, 2, and 3 correctly highlight their differing views on socialism, the ideal state, and methods of resistance. Statement 4 is also accurate; while both opposed untouchability, Gandhi aimed at reforming the caste system within its framework, whereas Bose advocated for its complete abolition. However, statement 5 is not entirely accurate. While both were critical of communism, Bose's admiration for certain aspects of Fascist discipline, as evidenced in his writings, complicates a blanket rejection of Fascism.  Therefore, only four statements accurately represent their ideological differences.



**3. Consider the following figures associated with the Indian National Congress and their roles:**

1.  A.O. Hume:  Instrumental in the Congress's formation.
2.  Womesh Chandra Bonnerjee:  First President of the Indian National Congress.
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale:  A prominent leader who advocated for Swaraj within the British Empire.
4.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak: A leader known for his nationalist views and participation in the Home Rule Movement.
5.  Annie Besant:  A prominent figure who led the Home Rule Movement alongside Tilak, but whose relationship with the INC was complex.

How many of the above individuals played significant roles in shaping the Indian National Congress or the broader nationalist movement, as accurately described?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (c)


**Explanation:**

All five individuals played significant and accurately described roles. A.O. Hume's pivotal role in the Congress's founding is well-established (1). Womesh Chandra Bonnerjee's presidency at the first session is a historical fact (2). Gokhale's advocacy for Swaraj within the Empire is accurately depicted (3). Tilak's significant contribution to the nationalist movement and his involvement in the Home Rule Movement are also accurately represented (4).  Annie Besant's leadership in the Home Rule Movement and her complex, albeit significant, relationship with the INC is accurately stated (5).  Therefore, the correct answer is (c).



**4. Consider the following regarding the responses of the Indian National Congress to World War II:**

1.  The Congress initially offered conditional support to the British war effort, contingent upon certain political concessions.
2.  Gandhi advocated for unconditional support to the Allied powers due to his opposition to Fascism.
3.  Subhas Chandra Bose and some leftist elements within the Congress favored exploiting Britain's difficulties to launch a mass movement for independence.
4.  The Cripps Mission, while offering some concessions, ultimately failed to satisfy the Congress due to its continued emphasis on dominion status rather than complete independence.
5.  The Congress Working Committee's resignation from provincial ministries in 1939 signaled its rejection of British policies and the lack of meaningful Indian participation in the war.

How many of these statements correctly reflect the Indian National Congress's multifaceted response to World War II?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five statements accurately describe the Congress's varied responses. The conditional offer of support (1), Gandhi's position on unconditional support (2), Bose's contrasting view (3), the Cripps Mission's failure (4), and the resignation of Congress ministries (5) are all historically accurate. The diversity of opinion within the Congress and the complexities of its relationship with the British government during the war are accurately reflected in these statements. Therefore, the correct answer is (c).


**5. Consider the following statements about the Swarajist Party and the No-Changers within the Indian National Congress:**

1.  The Swarajists advocated for participation in legislative councils as a means of furthering the nationalist cause.
2.  The No-Changers primarily focused on constructive work and non-cooperation with the British government.
3.  The differences between these two groups led to a significant split within the Congress, mirroring the 1907 Surat Split.
4.  The Swarajists' activities in legislative councils included consistent obstructionist tactics to hinder the government's functioning.
5.  Mahatma Gandhi initially opposed the Swarajists' council entry strategy but later reconciled with them, recognizing the value of their work.

How many of the above statements accurately describe the dynamics between the Swarajist Party and the No-Changers?

(a) Only three
(b) Only four
(c) All five
(d) Only two


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Four of the statements are correct. The Swarajists' strategy of council entry (1), the No-Changers' focus on constructive work (2), the Swarajists' obstructionist tactics (4), and Gandhi's initial opposition followed by reconciliation (5) are all accurate. However, statement 3 is incorrect; while there were significant disagreements, the conflict between the Swarajists and No-Changers did not result in a major split like the 1907 Surat Split.  The two groups ultimately found ways to cooperate within the Congress framework. Therefore, only four statements accurately describe the dynamics between these groups.

**1. Consider the following:**

1.  The Champaran Satyagraha, led by Mahatma Gandhi, addressed the grievances of indigo farmers.
2.  The Tinkathia system mandated indigo cultivation on a specific portion of farmers' land.
3.  The first communist government in India was established in Kerala.
4.  The Anglo-Nepal War occurred during the reign of Lord Hastings.
5.  The Indian Councils Act of 1909, also known as the Morley-Minto Reforms, introduced limited electoral representation.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect aspects of India's history and political development during the British Raj and its aftermath?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha, initiated in 1917, was Mahatma Gandhi's first major Satyagraha campaign in India, focusing on the plight of indigo farmers exploited by British planters under the oppressive Tinkathia system.

Statement 2 is correct.  The Tinkathia system in Champaran forced farmers to cultivate indigo on 3/20th of their land, regardless of their preference or the suitability of their land for indigo cultivation. This system was a key factor contributing to the widespread agrarian distress that Gandhi addressed.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The first communist government in India was established in the state of Kerala in 1957, not under the British Raj.

Statement 4 is correct. The Anglo-Nepal War took place between 1814 and 1816, during the Governor-Generalship of Lord Hastings. This war significantly shaped the British presence in the Himalayan region.

Statement 5 is correct. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, part of the Indian Councils Act, introduced a system of limited electoral representation, marking a significant step towards greater Indian participation in governance, albeit with considerable limitations and restrictions.


Therefore, only three statements (1, 2, and 4) are entirely accurate.  The other two contain inaccuracies or require significant qualification.



**2. Consider the following:**

1.  The Surat Session of the Indian National Congress in 1907 witnessed a major split between the Moderates and Extremists.
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, advocated for "Swaraj."
3.  Lord Curzon's administration in India was compared to that of Aurangzeb by Gopal Krishna Gokhale.
4.  The Vernacular Press Act of 1878, enacted during Lord Lytton's tenure, restricted the freedom of the Indian press.
5.  The first Law Minister of India was Dr. B.R. Ambedkar.

How many of the statements above accurately describe events and figures associated with the Indian freedom struggle and the British Raj?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All five

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Surat Session of 1907 marked a significant turning point in the Indian National Congress, witnessing a major split between the more moderate and the more radical elements within the organization. This division significantly impacted the movement's strategy and effectiveness.

Statement 2 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent early leader of the Indian National Congress, was a strong advocate for "Swaraj," or self-rule, a key goal of the Indian independence movement.  His advocacy for Swaraj helped shape the movement's long-term objectives.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Lord Curzon's administration was indeed criticized for its authoritarian nature, it was B.G. Tilak, not Gokhale, who drew parallels between Curzon's policies and those of the Mughal emperor Aurangzeb.

Statement 4 is correct. The Vernacular Press Act of 1878, implemented during Lord Lytton's tenure, imposed restrictions on the Indian-language press, aiming to curb nationalist sentiments expressed through publications.  This act reflects the British government's efforts to control the flow of information.

Statement 5 is incorrect.  While Dr. B.R. Ambedkar played a crucial role in drafting the Indian Constitution, the first Law Minister of independent India was Kailash Nath Katju.


Thus, three statements (1, 2, and 4) accurately reflect historical realities.  The other two contain factual inaccuracies.


**3. Consider the following:**

1.  The Ryotwari system of land revenue was primarily implemented in the Bombay and Madras Presidencies.
2.  The Mahalwari system was introduced in parts of northern India, with variations in its implementation.
3.  The Permanent Settlement, primarily implemented in Bengal, granted proprietary rights to zamindars.
4.  The Izaredari system, implemented by Warren Hastings, involved assigning revenue collection to contractors.
5.  The British consistently supported social reforms in India to promote modernization.

How many of the statements above correctly describe British land revenue systems and their impact on Indian society?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 2, 3, and 4
(c) 1, 3, and 5
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Ryotwari system, a direct revenue collection system from individual cultivators, was primarily implemented in the Bombay and Madras Presidencies, although with variations and regional adaptations.

Statement 2 is correct. The Mahalwari system, which involved revenue assessment at the village level (mahal), was implemented across parts of northern India, particularly in the North-Western Provinces and Punjab, with variations in its application.

Statement 3 is correct. The Permanent Settlement, introduced by Lord Cornwallis, granted proprietary rights to Zamindars in Bengal and Bihar, although this system had significant long-term consequences and contributed to land inequality.

Statement 4 is correct.  Warren Hastings implemented the Izaredari system, a farming system where revenue collection was contracted out to individuals or groups, often leading to exploitation and corruption.

Statement 5 is incorrect.  British policy towards social reforms was inconsistent and often driven by their own political and economic interests. While some reforms were supported initially, this support often waned as the British increasingly sought to maintain social order and their own dominance.


Therefore, statements 1, 2, 3, and 4 accurately describe aspects of British land revenue policies. Statement 5 presents an oversimplified and inaccurate view of British involvement in social reform.



**4. Consider the following individuals:**

1.  M.C. Setalvad
2.  Rafi Ahmad Kidwai
3.  Kailash Nath Katju
4.  Dr. B.R. Ambedkar

How many of the above served as Law Ministers of India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Kailash Nath Katju served as the first Law Minister of India.  Dr. B.R. Ambedkar was instrumental in drafting the Constitution but did not serve as a Law Minister. Therefore, only one of the individuals listed definitively served as Law Minister. However,  M.C. Setalvad later served as India's Attorney General, and Rafi Ahmad Kidwai held other ministerial portfolios, creating plausible distractors.  The question's difficulty lies in the subtle distinction between the roles of Law Minister and other legal or political positions held by these individuals.  Therefore, only two individuals listed held high legal positions in the Indian government.



**5. Consider the following statements regarding the Indian National Congress:**

1.  The Congress was founded in 1885 with the primary goal of achieving complete independence.
2.  The Congress split into Moderate and Extremist wings at the Surat Session of 1907.
3.  Mahatma Gandhi played a significant role in leading the Congress during the Indian independence movement.
4.  The Congress consistently opposed all forms of violence during the freedom struggle.
5.  The Congress actively supported the Khilafat Movement.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect the history and actions of the Indian National Congress?

(a) Only two
(b) Only three
(c) Only four
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Congress's long-term goal evolved toward complete independence, its initial aims were more moderate, focusing on reforms within the existing British framework.

Statement 2 is correct. The Surat Split of 1907 dramatically divided the Congress into Moderate and Extremist factions, reflecting differing strategies and approaches to achieving self-rule.

Statement 3 is correct. Mahatma Gandhi's leadership was pivotal in transforming the Congress into a mass movement and significantly reshaping its strategies during the independence struggle.

Statement 4 is incorrect. While Gandhi championed non-violence, the Congress encompassed diverse viewpoints, and some factions employed or supported different methods of resistance.

Statement 5 is correct. The Congress initially supported the Khilafat Movement, demonstrating its willingness to collaborate with other groups to achieve broader political goals.


Therefore, only three statements (2, 3, and 5) accurately reflect aspects of the Indian National Congress's history.  The other two contain inaccuracies or require significant nuance.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria:


**1. Consider the following:**

1.  The establishment of the Pusa agriculture college.
2.  The interpretation of "ultimate self-government" as a political ideal.
3.  Leading the invasion of Tibet.
4.  The appointment of a Police Commission.

How many of the above are associated with the administrative actions or policies of Lord Curzon during his tenure as Viceroy of India?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:** All four statements accurately reflect aspects of Lord Curzon's actions and policies. He established the Pusa agricultural college to advance agricultural education and research. He interpreted the concept of "ultimate self-government" within the context of British imperial rule, advocating for a gradual approach.  His administration oversaw a British military invasion of Tibet in 1903-1904. Finally, he appointed a Police Commission to reform and improve the Indian police force.  Therefore, all four actions are directly linked to his viceroyalty.  There are no inaccuracies or misleading elements in the statements to create difficulty; the challenge lies in the factual recall of multiple associated actions.


**2. Consider the following personalities:**

1.  Rabindranath Tagore
2.  Madan Mohan Malaviya
3.  Subhash Chandra Bose
4.  Jawaharlal Nehru

How many of these individuals were actively involved in the Indian independence movement, demonstrating a significant contribution beyond purely educational or reformist roles?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** While all four individuals were important figures in their respective fields, only three played significant direct roles in the independence movement beyond educational reforms.  Rabindranath Tagore, though critical at times, engaged in nationalist discourse and activities.  Madan Mohan Malaviya's involvement was primarily through educational and social reform organizations that indirectly aided the independence movement, not a directly political role. Subhash Chandra Bose and Jawaharlal Nehru were central leaders of the Indian National Congress, directly involved in political strategies and negotiations. Therefore, three of the four were directly active participants in the independence struggle.


**3. Consider the following:**

1.  The Ancient Monuments Preservation Act, 1904.
2.  The Ancient and Historical Monuments and Archaeological Sites and Remains (Declaration of National Importance) Act, 1951.
3.  The recommendation for the establishment of the National Mission for Manuscripts (NMM).

How many of the above legislative acts or initiatives fall under the purview of the Archaeological Survey of India (ASI)?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** The ASI's mandate includes the preservation and protection of historical monuments and relics. Both the 1904 and 1951 acts directly relate to this responsibility, providing legal frameworks for the protection of archaeological sites and remains. The ASI has also been involved in recommending the establishment of initiatives like the NMM, demonstrating its broader role in cultural preservation. All three fall under its area of responsibility or influence.  The question's difficulty arises from requiring knowledge of specific legislation related to the ASI, which is not commonly known.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the Non-Cooperation Movement:**

1.  It involved significant participation from the urban Muslim population.
2.  It was concurrently active with the Khilafat Movement.
3.  The Chauri Chaura incident led to its suspension.
4.  It was primarily led by Motilal Nehru.

How many of the above statements are factually accurate regarding the Non-Cooperation Movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:** Statements 1, 2, and 3 are accurate. The Non-Cooperation Movement saw substantial participation from urban Muslims, particularly due to its connection with the Khilafat Movement.  The two movements ran concurrently, sharing some goals and participants. The violence at Chauri Chaura was a key factor in Gandhi's decision to suspend the Non-Cooperation Movement. However, statement 4 is incorrect; the movement was primarily led by Mahatma Gandhi, not Motilal Nehru.  The question's difficulty stems from the need to distinguish between the key leader and other important participants within the movement, and to recall the event which ultimately led to its suspension.


**5. Consider the following works of literature and their authors:**

1.  *Gora* – Bankim Chandra Chatterjee
2.  *Anand Math* – Rabindranath Tagore
3.  *Durgesh Nandini* – Bankim Chandra Chatterjee

How many of the above author-work pairings are correctly matched?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**  *Durgesh Nandini* and *Anand Math* were authored by Bankim Chandra Chatterjee, making that pairing correct.  However,  *Gora* was written by Rabindranath Tagore, not Bankim Chandra Chatterjee.  Therefore, only two of the pairings are correct.  The question's difficulty is derived from the deliberate inclusion of plausible but incorrect pairings of well-known authors and their works, requiring precise knowledge of each author's literary output.  The close relationship between the incorrect and correct answers enhances the difficulty.


**6. Consider the following individuals associated with the early nationalist movement:**

1.  Dadabhai Naoroji, known for his work on the "drain of wealth" theory.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a prominent leader of the Home Rule movement.
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a staunch advocate for immediate complete independence.

How many of the above statements accurately describe the contributions of these individuals to the early nationalist movement?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Dadabhai Naoroji's contribution to the "drain of wealth" theory is well-documented. Bal Gangadhar Tilak's leadership of the Home Rule movement is also a known fact. However, statement 3 is inaccurate. Gopal Krishna Gokhale, while a significant early nationalist leader, advocated for a more gradual approach to self-rule, not immediate complete independence, unlike more radical contemporaries. Thus, only two statements are entirely accurate.  The question tests factual knowledge about prominent figures and their specific contributions, including a nuanced understanding of their political approaches.  The inclusion of a partially true statement about Gokhale adds to the complexity.

**7. Consider the following statements about Lord Wellesley's tenure as Governor-General:**

1. He implemented the Subsidiary Alliance system.
2. He aimed to counteract alliances with Tipu Sultan.
3. He conquered Sindh.

How many of the above statements accurately reflect Lord Wellesley's actions and policies?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** Lord Wellesley is known for his implementation of the Subsidiary Alliance system, a key aspect of his expansionist foreign policy. He also actively worked to counter the alliances and influence of Tipu Sultan, leading to military confrontations. However, the conquest of Sindh did not occur during his time; it happened later.  Therefore, only two statements are correct.  The question tests specific knowledge of Wellesley's policies and actions, using a closely related but incorrect statement about Sindh to increase the challenge.


**8. Consider the following individuals and their association with the Non-Cooperation Movement:**

1.  Vallabhbhai Patel
2.  C. Rajagopalachari
3.  Sardar Patel
4.  Jawaharlal Nehru

How many of the above individuals were actively involved in the Non-Cooperation Movement?

(b) Only two
(c) Three
(d) All four

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**  Vallabhbhai Patel, C. Rajagopalachari, and Jawaharlal Nehru were all key figures in the Non-Cooperation Movement, actively participating in its various aspects.  Since Sardar Patel is the same person as Vallabhbhai Patel, all four names reference individuals involved in the movement.  The question's difficulty lies in recognizing the redundancy and ensuring a clear understanding of the prominent leaders involved.


**9. Consider the following statements about the impact of the rediscovery of India's past on the nationalist movement:**

1. It fostered a sense of shared national identity.
2. It exclusively promoted Hindu communalism.
3. It inspired artistic and literary movements.

How many of the above accurately describe the effects of the rediscovery of India's past?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:** The rediscovery of India's past played a significant role in fostering a sense of shared national identity, uniting diverse groups under a common historical narrative.  It also inspired artistic and literary movements, as seen in the Bengal School of Art and the works of Rabindranath Tagore. However, the statement that it *exclusively* promoted Hindu communalism is incorrect; while Hindu elements featured prominently, the rediscovery also influenced other religious and cultural groups and their nationalist narratives. Therefore, only two statements are accurate.  The question tests the understanding of a complex historical process, incorporating a misleading statement to increase difficulty.


**10. Consider the following: **

1.  The Bengal School of Art.
2.  The creation of paintings.

(b) Only two

(d) All four
